        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Rizzo is one of the more interesting fantasy options entering this season. He's got nothing to prove in the minors, and he's only blocked by Bryan LaHair at first base. Rizzo struggled in his debut last season -- striking out 30.1% of the time -- but he completely tore up Triple-A league to the tune of .331/.404/.652. On the other hand, that league and park was offense-friendly and some scouts have whispered about a long swing. Now in Chicago, Rizzo will make an interesting gamble in the late rounds. The strikeouts bear watching, but he's got strong power potential. (Chris Cwik)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Rizzo has nothing more to prove in the minors and deserves a shot at a starting job this season. He's an interesting late round pick now that he only has to beat out Bryan LaHair.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>In just his age-22 season, Anthony Rizzo clapped 15 homers through 368 plate appearances (a pace of 24 homers per 600 PA) and hit a solid .285/.342/.463 slash. Can he translate that 116 wRC+ into even better numbers in 2013? He should. Though Cubs fans may feel he cooled off as the season went, his numbers stuck pretty close to the 110 wRC+ mark even after his hot start. Perhaps the best news was that a change in his swing mechanics seemed to have fixed some of his contact problems, which bodes well for his batting average. In his age-23 season, Rizzo will get full-time PA and should go early or expensive in most any draft. If not, make sure you are the one who has him. He may not be the best first baseman in fantasy, but at worst, he ranks in the back of the top tier. (<a href="https://twitter.com/BradleyWoodrum">Bradley Woodrum</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Rizzo had impressive numbers as a 22-year-old. He will get prime treatment both in the form of lineup placement and playing time. Because he is not fully proven just yet, he likely ranks as the cheapest of the top tier first basemen.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>There's a lot of bellyaching in certain circles about the season Anthony Rizzo put up in 2013. Yes, he only hit .233. And yeah, he only hit 23 homers. But he did something very important, too. He maintained strikeout and isolated slugging numbers that were better than league -- for the second year in a row. Guess what the average batting average was for a qualified batter that did those things last season? .285. Coincidentally, that's the exact batting average Rizzo had in 2012. The point is that Rizzo has power, and he makes contact better than the league rate, and that combo is rare. Let's say you don't want to pencil him for a .285 batting average next year -- maybe you think he's just not a line drive hitter -- .233 is absurdly low for a player with his skillset, and his .258 batting average on balls in play is mostly to blame. Consider he's only 24, so he's pre-peak with regards to his power, too. Just a little boost, and Rizzo's within a chip shot and a ducksnort of .280 and 30 homers. Two players hit those benchmarks last year -- Chris Davis and Paul Goldschmidt. If you can't afford the first two, consider the bargain bin version in this year's drafts. (<a href="http://www.twitter.com/enosarris">Eno Sarris</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>For a guy that struck out less than league average and showed good power, Rizzo got a lot of grief for his 2013 season. Make others' pain your gain by buying low on the Cubbie slugger.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>"Just a little boost, and Rizzo's within a chip shot and a ducksnort of .280 and 30 homers." That's how last year's forward-looking player capsule on Anthony Rizzo ended. Rizzo hit .286 with 32 homers, so technically, the author (me) was wrong. But it's obvious, at least now, that the Cubs first baseman is strong with the plate discipline, can make contact better than your average big leaguer, and can hang with any regular first baseman in the power department. Considering he's only 25 years old, and that Cubs lineup is set to get better around him, there's actually still room for growth. Why shouldn't a guy that hits .280+ with 30+ homers and an on-base percentage near .400 drive in 100 runners and score a bunch more? Last year, with those numbers, he drove in 89 and scored 78. Give him thirty more runs and RBI combined this past season, and he would have been the <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/end-of-season-fantasy-rankings-auction-values-first-basemen/">fourth-best first baseman</a> in fantasy baseball. And the three above him are all significantly older, with one -- Victor Martinez -- offering significant risk for regression. Rizzo is worth a hefty investment this year, considering he could grow in all categories along with this team and should end up a top-three first baseman when the dust settles on 2015. (Eno Sarris)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>The best thing about Anthony Rizzo's best season is that he did it at 25 years old and his statistically history pointed to this breakout. He has room to grow -- and the team around him looks like it's improving -- and the work was believable, so treat him like a top-three first baseman in the league this coming year. Rock solid.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>It's hard to believe at 26 years old, Rizzo is one of the more senior members of the Cubs lineup. He might also be the best all-around hitter in said lineup. He finished 2015 with a .278/.387/.512 triple slash, and posted career-bests in on-base percentage, runs scored, RBIs, and stolen bases. He led the National League in games played and plate appearances, and led the majors in a dubious category, as he was hit by 30 pitches during the season. This was his third full season, and he posted a career-best in strikeout percentage. For a player who hits for the kind of power Rizzo does, that's impressive. Rizzo is heading into his age-26 season, and he only appears to be getting better. He is the anchor in the young Cubs' lineup with hitters like Javier Baez, Kris Bryant, Kyle Schwarber, and Jorge Soler. The addition of Jason Heyward and a year of maturation by the youngsters could lead to Rizzo getting more RBI opportunities. He hits lefties so well that he doesn't need to be lifted late in games for a right-handed pinch hitter. He's already in the elite class of first baseman, and he's gunning for guys like Paul Goldschmidt and Joey Votto. It's hard to imagine Rizzo improving on his last two seasons, but with a loaded Cubs' roster, more runs and RBI could foster such growth at the very least. (Dustin Nosler)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Rizzo saw some of his numbers dip slightly, but he was still a top four MVP finisher in the National League. He finished in the top five among first basemen in the following categories: home runs (31), runs batted in (101), runs scored (94), doubles (38), stolen bases (17) and on-base percentage (.387).</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Anthony Rizzo has spent the last three seasons establishing himself as one of the most consistent players in all of baseball. His home run totals in the last three seasons feature marks of 32, 31, and 32. His on-base percentage has gone .386, .387, and .385 thanks, in part, to a walk rate of 11.9%, 11.1%, and 10.9%. His park-adjusted offense was 55% above league average in 2014 before falling 45% above league average in each of the last two years. His isolated power in 2016 came in at .252, representing the best mark of his career. His strikeout rate remained somewhat favorable with a 16.0% mark. Adding to the intrigue are his splits against left-handed pitching, which continued to fall in his favor. While he mashed righties, he actually struck out less against southpaws and still managed a .205 isolated power against them. His 17 steals in 2015 were likely an outlier, as he swiped only three in 2016, but he does add a bit of value as a base runner at the first base position. Overall, Rizzo represents one of the premier options at the first base position. He's a 30 homer guy with constant opportunities to knock in runs with the lineup in front of him. (Randy Holt)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Anthony Rizzo represents as consistent a force as there is, both at the first base position and in all of baseball. With an on-base percentage that has found its way around the .385 mark and over 30 home runs in each of the last three seasons, Rizzo continues to represent one of the best at first base.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>

        //            }

        hideSO('so6');

        }
        else {
            panelo.style.display = 'none';
            document.getElementById('soa6').style.fontWeight = 'normal';
        }
    }

    function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    function setPart(t) {

            $(this).qtip(

		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use

		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },

		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,

		    },
